13/10/23, 4:22â€¯pm - Rajjo: I am an ex-employee of Newgen. I hated the job. Firstly, they work on outdated technolgies. You really cannot learn anything new in a company like this. They are not open to any new ideas. Also, they make you stay a lot longer as compared to your working hours and you will have to work even on some weekends. Although it is okay when sometimes it is really needed, but the thing is that the management at this firm is very unresponsive to its employeesâ€™ problems. There is a lot of hierarchy and nobody cares even if you are not feeling well, you have some urgent problem in your family or whatsoever. The only benefits of working in this company are : free transport (though less number of routes), free evening snacks and exposure (you may get more work and responsibilites than you want).

In a nutshell, on weighing the two sides, I would not suggest this compny to anyone.

27/01/24, 12:53â€¯pm - Abhishek Mittal: As a Digital Forensics and Incident Response (DFIR) analyst, you have been assigned to investigate a compromised computer system. During your investigation, you've discovered a text file that seems to contain important evidence. It's your responsibility to identify and extract sensitive information from this file, which could be crucial in understanding the extent of the incident.

Your task is to create a script that will meticulously scan the entire text file to locate and extract the following types of sensitive data:

Social Security Numbers (SSNs) in the format XXX-XX-XXXX (e.g., 123-45-6789).
Valid Credit card numbers in the format XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX as per luhn algorithm (e.g., CC no 1234-5678-9012-3456 without hyphens 1234567812345678).
Email addresses.
Phone numbers in the format (123) 456-7890.

After identifying these data, your next task is to capture the last character of each of the above type of sensitive data in their original order of appearance. These characters will be used to form the Flag in the following example format: HQ8{Extracted_Characters}.
Note: Include the script developed to solve this quest in the report.
27/01/24, 12:57â€¯pm - Aryan Prajapati: https://talentbattle.us10.list-manage.com/track/click?u=35d77a9012e6580c16a143c19&id=14a5987008&e=a45e10ebe7

27/01/24, 1:07â€¯pm - Aryan Prajapati: import re

def is_valid_ipv4(ip):
    # Regular expression for matching valid IPv4 addresses starting with "92.85."
    ipv4_pattern = re.compile( r'^92\.85\.(25[0-5]|2[0-4][0-9]|[0-1]?[0-9][0-9]?)\.(25[0-5]|2[0-4][0-9]|[0-1]?[0-9][0-9]?)$')
    return ipv4_pattern.match(ip)

def is_c2_ipv6(ip):
    # Regular expression for matching C2 server IPv6 addresses ith the specified pattern
    ipv6_pattern = re.compile(r'^2510:a5:[\da-fA-F]{1,4}:[\da-fA-F]{1,4}:[\da-fA-F]{1,4}$')
    return ipv6_pattern.match(ip)

def process_ip_addresses(file_path):
    flagged_characters = []

    with open(file_path, 'r') as file:
        for line in file:
            # Remove leading and trailing whitespaces
            ip = line.strip()

            # Check if it is a valid IPv4 or a C2 server IPv6 address
            if is_valid_ipv4(ip):
                print(f'Malicious IPv4: {ip}')
                flagged_characters.append(ip[-1])
            if is_c2_ipv6(ip):
                print(f'C2 Server IPv6: {ip}')
                flagged_characters.append(ip[-1])

    # Print the flagged characters after the loop
    print(flagged_characters)

    # Construct the Flag
    flag = 'HQ8{' + ''.join(flagged_characters) + '}'
    print(f'Flag: {flag}')

# Replace 'path/to/your/file.txt' with the actual path to your file
process_ip_addresses('C:\\Users\\Abhay\\Downloads\\Semantic+Safari_cf612e5b25b23db\\ip.lst')
